6 Classification The equipment has the following classifications:
- Type of protection against electric shock: Class I
- Degree of protection against electric shock (Patient
connections): No applied part specified.
- Degree of protection against harmful ingress of water or
particulate matter: Ordinary equipment (IPX0)
- Methods of sterilization: The equipment is not intended
to be sterilized by operator.
- Degree of safety application for use in an oxygen
environment: Not applicable.
- Mode of operation: Continuous operation
7 Identification, markings and
documents
Markings and instructions related to the safety shall be in
a language which is acceptable in the country in which
the equipment is to be sold. Markings and instructions in
English were evaluated in this test report.

General product information and other remarks:
The equipment is indicated for use in general projection radiographic applications wherever conventional
screen-film systems or CR systems may be used. This device is not intended for mammographic
applications.
The equipment consists of digital flat panel X-ray detector and power supply. The digital flat panel X-ray
detector is intended to receive its power from the power supply, model HAD1717M and connect using
special connector style. Therefore, the specified power supply is considered as another part of the same
ME equipment in this test report.
The equipment is generally used with X-ray equipment / system including operating PC in end-use
application. Refer to below set-up diagrams which are intended by the manufacturer.
Based on above set-up diagrams, further consideration shall be checked as following when the equipment
is used in the end-use application.
- The suitability of the mounting means shall be tested and evaluated.
- The compliance shall be tested and evaluated when the equipment constitutes as ME system in the
end-use application.
- X-ray equipment / system shall be powered from separate mains supply which complies with IEC
60601-1.
- Operation PC shall be powered from separate mains supply which complies with IEC 60601-1,
IEC 60950-1 or IEC 62368-1.
All testing was conducted with the PC submitted by manufacturer (Type: Latitude, manufactured by Dell
Inc.), since it doesn’t provide in the product package, Therefore, the equipment should be considered
whether the compliance needs to be additionally tested evaluated, when it constitutes as the ME system
with other equipment which is not verified in this test report.
Model differences:
- The main model is HAD1717MC.
- The variant HAD1717MG is identical to main model HAD1717MC except for model name and
scintillator, refer to technical specification table below.
- The variant HAD1717VC is identical to main model HAD1717MC except for model name and target
object (for veterinary only).
Unless otherwise specified, all testing was conducted with main model HAD1717MC as representative.

INSULATION DIAGRAM CONVENTIONS and GUIDANCE:
A measured value must be provided in the value columns for the device under evaluation. The symbol >
(greater than sign) must not be used. Switch-mode power supplies must be re-evaluated in the device
under evaluation therefore N/A must not be used with a generic statement that the component is
certified.
Insulation diagram is a graphical representation of equipment insulation barriers, protective impedance
and protective earthing. If feasible, use the following conventions to generate the diagram:
- All isolation barriers are identified by letters between separate parts of diagram, for example separate transformer
windings, optocouplers, wire insulation, creepage and clearance distances.
- Parts connected to earth with large dots are protectively earthed. Other connections to earth are functional
- Applied parts are extended beyond the equipment enclosure and terminated with an arrow.
- Parts accessible to the operator only are extended outside of the enclosure but are not terminated with an arrow.

Attachment - Software – IEC 62304:2006+AMD1:2015 —
4.3 [A, B, C] Software safety classification —
a) The MANUFACTURER assigns to each SOFTWARE
SYSTEM a software safety class according to the RISK
of HARM to the patient, operator, or other people
resulting from a HAZARDOUS SITUATION to which the
SOFTWARE SYSTEM can contribute in a worst-case-
scenario
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-010), chapter 1
P
The SOFTWARE SYSTEM is software safety class A if: —
– the SOFTWARE SYSTEM not contribute to a
HAZARDOUS SITUATION; or
Classified as software class B. N/A
– the SOFTWARE SYSTEM contribute to a HAZARDOUS
SITUATION which does not result in unacceptable
RISK after consideration of RISK CONTROL measures
external to the SOFTWARE SYSTEM
N/A
The SOFTWARE SYSTEM is software safety class B if: —
– the SOFTWARE SYSTEM contribute to a HAZARDOUS
SITUATION which results in unacceptable RISK after
consideration of RISK CONTROL measures external to
the SOFTWARE SYSTEM and the resulting possible
HARM is non-SERIOUS INJURY
P
The SOFTWARE SYSTEM is software safety class C if: —
– the SOFTWARE SYSTEM contribute to a HAZARDOUS
SITUATION which results in unacceptable RISK after
consideration of RISK CONTROL measures external to
the SOFTWARE SYSTEM and the resulting possible
HARM is death or SERIOUS INJURY
Classified as software class B. N/A
For a SOFTWARE SYSTEM initially classified as
software safety class B or C, the MANUFACTURER
has implemented additional RISK CONTROL measures
external to the SOFTWARE SYSTEM and subsequently
has assigned a new software safety classification to
the SOFTWARE SYSTEM
N/A
c) The MANUFACTURER documents the software
safety class assigned to each SOFTWARE SYSTEM in
the RISK MANAGEMENT FILE
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-010), chapter 1
P
d) When a SOFTWARE SYSTEM is decomposed into
SOFTWARE ITEMS, and when a SOFTWARE ITEM is
decomposed into further SOFTWARE ITEMS, such
SOFTWARE ITEMS inherit the software safety
classification of the original SOFTWARE ITEM (or
SOFTWARE SYSTEM) unless the MANUFACTURER
documents a rationale for classification into a
different software safety class
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-010), chapter 1
P

Page 148 of 165 Report No. REP042127
IEC 60601-1
Clause Requirement + Test Result - Remark Verdict
TRF No. IEC60601_1U
A rationale explains how the new SOFTWARE ITEMS
are segregated so that they may be classified
separately
P
e) The MANUFACTURER documents the software
safety class of each SOFTWARE ITEM if that class is
different from the class of the SOFTWARE ITEM from
which it was created by decomposition
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-010), chapter 1
P
f) When applied to a group of SOFTWARE ITEMS, the
MANUFACTURER uses the PROCESSES and TASKS
which are required by the classification of the
highest-classified SOFTWARE ITEM in the group
unless the MANUFACTURER documents in the RISK
MANAGEMENT FILE a rationale for using a lower
classification
Software validation report
(A-TCF-5-010), chapter 1
P
g) Class C requirements apply for each SOFTWARE
SYSTEM, until a software safety class is assigned
Classified as software class B. N/A

Testing shall be carried out using a DETACHABLE
POWER SUPPLY CORD as provided or specified
(length and cross-sectional area as per the
Canadian Electrical Code, Part I) by the
MANUFACTURER.
P
The test current shall have the following
characteristics:
— for cord-connected equipment, twice the rating
of the attachment plug cap, but not less than 40 A;
— for equipment for permanent connection to the
supply, twice the rating of the fuse that is required
by the Canadian Electrical Code, Part I for the
branch circuit to which the equipment is
connected, up to 250 A; and
— 500 A for equipment for permanent connection
to the supply when a branch circuit fused at over
250 A is required.
See appended table 8.6.4 in
part 1 original test report No.
REP042127.
P
Compliance is checked by the following test:
— for test currents up to 500 A, the measured
potential drop shall not exceed 4 V;
— for equipment that requires branch circuit fusing
over 250 A, the measured potential drop multiplied
by the required fusing and divided by 250 shall not
exceed 4 V;
— there shall be no melting of any metal in the
bond and no heating or burning that is likely to
create a fire hazard; and
— the time duration— the time duration for testing
is indicated in Table 8.6.4A:
N/A
P

ME EQUIPMENT is rated dc. N/A

Attachment 2
National Differences
Page 13 of 33
Report No.: REP042127
IEC60601_1U ATTACHMENT
Clause Requirement + Test Result - Remark Verdict
Note: When protective earth is relied on as a
MEANS OF PROTECTION, the test current is
determined based on the location where a fault
could occur. If the prospective fault is in the mains
supply circuit prior to the overcurrent protection
included in the ME EQUIPMENT, the test current
for that part of the protective earth circuit is based
on the rating of the external overcurrent protection
included in the building infrastructure or specified
in the ACCOMPANYING DOCUMENTS (two times
the interrupt rating of the external overcurrent
protection). If the prospective fault is in the mains
supply circuit after the overcurrent protection
included in the ME EQUIPMENT, the
test current is based on the rating of the
overcurrent protection included in the ME
EQUIPMENT (two times the interrupt rating of the
ME EQUIPMENT overcurrent protection). In either
case, the minimum test current is 40 A.
The voltage drop between the parts described is
measured and the impedance determined from the
current and voltage drop.
If the measured impedance is within the permitted
limit, either the impedance measurement is then

repeated using a current source with a no-load
voltage sufficient to deliver the specified current
into the total impedance, or the current-carrying
ability of the relevant protective earth conductor
and protective earth connection is confirmed by
checking that their cross-sectional area is at least
equal to that of the relevant current-carrying
conductors.
N/A
8.7 LEAKAGE CURRENTS and PATIENT AUXILIARY CURRENTS P
8.7.3 Allowable values P
[Add the following paragraph]
Allowable values shall be in accordance with the
Canadian Electrical Code, Part I.

power supply cable used. However, the characteristics of the separating transformer
need to be carefully selected, taking into account the variations in the load current of

SYSTEM remains within the limits specified for the equipment.

Use of uncertainty of measurement for decisions on conformity (decision rule) :
No decision rule is specified by the IEC standard, when comparing the measurement result with the
applicable limit according to the specification in that standard. The decisions on conformity are made
without applying the measurement uncertainty (“simple acceptance” decision rule, previously known as
“accuracy method”).

accreditation requirements apply)
Information on uncertainty of measurement:
The uncertainties of measurement are calculated by the laboratory based on application of criteria given
by OD-5014 for test equipment and application of test methods, decision sheets and operational
procedures of IECEE.
IEC Guide 115 provides guidance on the application of measurement uncertainty principles and applying
the decision rule when reporting test results within IECEE scheme, noting that the reporting of the
measurement uncertainty for measurements is not necessary unless required by the test standard or
customer.
Calculations leading to the reported values are on file with the NCB and testing laboratory that conducted
the testing.

instructions in this manual closely. Become familiar with the safety precautions and usage procedures
for this Product. Note that the Product may differ slightly from the contents of this manual, depending
on individual Product specifications.

1.4 Warning
Symbols Descriptions
Environment of Use and Storage
 Follow the specified process of operation instruction written in this manual
for the safety of the users and patients.
Connection
 Do not connect the detector with anything other than specified. Otherwise, it
may result in fire or electric shock.
 To avoid the risk of electric shock, this detector must only be connected to
supply mains with protective earth.
 Avoid installing the system in such way that it is difficult for the operator to
disconnect the appliance plug.
 Do not touch Signal Input Part/Signal Output Part and the patient
simultaneously. There is a risk of electric shock from current leakage.
 Additional equipment connected to medical electrical equipment must
comply with the respective IEC or ISO standards. Furthermore, all
configurations shall comply with the requirements for medical electrical
systems. Anybody connecting additional equipment to medical electrical
equipment configures a medical system and is therefore responsible that
the system complies with the requirements for medical electrical systems.
Attention is drawn to the fact that local laws take priority over the above-
mentioned requirements.
 Equipment connected to the detector and in the patient environment must
be powered from a medically-isolated power source or must be a medically-
isolated device. Equipment powered from a non-isolated source can result
in chassis leakage currents exceeding safe levels. Chassis leakage current
created by an accessory or device connected to a non-isolated outlet may
add to the chassis leakage current of the detector.
Handling
 Always be sure to keep checking the condition of the system and the patient
to ensure they are normal during the use of the detector. If any problem is
found, take appropriate measures, such as stopping the operation of the
detector, as required.
 Never disassemble or modify the detector as it may result in fire or electric
shock.
 Also, since the detector incorporates parts that may cause electric shocks
and other hazardous parts, touching them may cause death or serious
injury.
 Do not hit or drop the detector. The detector may be damaged if it receives
a strong jolt, which may result in fire or electric shock if the detector is used
without being repaired

9
When Problem Occurs
 Should any of the following occur, immediately turn OFF the power of each
detector, unplug the power supply cord from the AC outlet, and contact
H&abyz Customer Service team or authorized agent.
 When there is smoke, odd smell or abnormal sound.
 When liquid has been spilled into the detector or a metal object has entered
through an opening.
 When the detector has been dropped and it is damaged.
Error Massages
 Messages about occur errors when using the detector are not output
directly from the software.
 It is provided in text format for use in upper-level software (see Section 1.5).
 For error message contents and actions, refer to the relevant upper level
software manual.
 If the Upper Level Software Manual does not work, contact your H&abyz
Customer Service team or authorized dealer.
Maintenance and Inspection
 For safety reasons, be sure to turn off the power of the detector when the
following inspections are going to be performed. Otherwise, it may result in
electric shock.
 When the detector is going to be cleaned, be sure to turn off the power of
each detector, and unplug the power cable from the AC outlet.
 Do not use any type of solvent, such as benzene. Otherwise, fire or electric
shock may result.
 Wear waterproof gloves to protect your hands from direct contact with IPA
(Isopropyl-alcohol) or any other liquid.
 Maintenance of the detector should be done by an authorized service
provider. If problem still cannot be corrected, it may result in fire or electric
shock.
 Replacing lithium batteries or fuel cells by inadequately trained personnel
could result in a hazardous situation.
Patients Contact
 Stay the Detector in a bucky, and do not position the patient on the detector
directly.

10
1.5 Caution
Symbols Descriptions
User Requirements
 This equipment should be only operated by users who have received
professional medical education and training, such as physicians,
radiologists, and other medical specialists.
Environment of Use and Storage
 Do not install the detector in a location with the conditions listed below.
Otherwise, it may result in failure or malfunction, cause fire or injury.
 Close to facilities where water is used.
 Where it will be exposed to direct sunlight.
 Close to air-conditioner or ventilation equipment.
 Close to heat source such as a heater.
 Prone to vibration
 Dusty environment.
 Saline or sulfurous environment.
 High temperature or humidity.
 Do not place the storage case in a location with the conditions listed
below
 Where the cable of the detector unit will be strongly pulled when the
detector is put into the case, otherwise, the cable may be damaged,
resulting in fire or electric shock.
 Where someone might get their foot caught in the cable.
Handling
 In order to prevent infection, please wipe the CFRP (Carbon Fiber
Reinforced Plastic) with a soft cloth moistened with IPA (Isopropyl-
alcohol) liquid. Wear waterproof gloves to protect your hands from direct
contact with IPA or any other liquid.
 For safety reasons, be sure to turn off the power of each equipment
when detector is not used.
Location of Cables
 Make sure all cables are located so that they cannot be stepped on,
tripped over, or otherwise subjected to damage or stress.

11
Maintenance and Inspection
 For safety reasons, be sure to inspect the detector before using it. In
addition, carry out a regular inspection at least once a year.
 If the detector is defective, do not disassemble the detector randomly.
Maintenance of the detector should be done by an authorized service
provider. Please contact H&abyz Customer Service team or authorized
agent.
 Be sure to check the user’s manual for replaceable components.

12
1.6 Safety Information
 General Safety
Preparation
 Be sure to connect the cables to the proper connectors. Otherwise, the detector may
malfunction or may be damaged.
Handling
 Handle the detector carefully, as it may become damaged if it is hit, dropped, or receives
a strong jolt.
 Be sure to use the detector on a flat place so it will not bend. Otherwise, the detector may
be damaged.
 Be sure to check the detector daily and confirm that it works properly. Sudden heating of
the room in cold areas will cause condensation to form on the detector. In this case, wait
until condensation disappears before performing exposure. If the detector is used with
condensation formed on it, problems may occur in the quality of the detector. When an
air-conditioner is going to be used, be sure to raise/lower the temperature gradually so
that a difference in temperature in the room and in the detector does not occur, to prevent
forming of condensation. Follow the recommended proper room temp.
 Do not use the detector near devices generating a strong magnetic field. Doing so may
produce image noise or artifacts.
 Keep the connectors free from being in contact with the patient.
 Connectors are intended to be connected to an external device and must follow IEC
standards.

13
 Do not apply excessive weight to the detector. Otherwise, the detector may be damaged
<Uniform Load : 150Kg over the whole area of sensor window >
<Local Load : 100Kg on 5 points areas of 40mm in diameter>
Disinfection and Cleaning
 Do not spray disinfectants or detergents on the detector.
 When cleaning the detector, be sure to turn off the power, and unplug the power cable
from the AC outlet.
 Do not use any flammable chemicals such as thinner, benzene for cleaning. Otherwise,
fire or electric shock may result.
 Wear waterproof gloves to protect your hands from direct contact with disinfectants or
detergents.
 Electrical Safety
 In compliance with IEC 60601-1, this medical equipment complies with the requirements
for Safety class I
 This system must be used in an environment complying with the requirements of the IEC.
 EMC (Electromagnetic Compatibility)
 Do not use any wireless devices, including cellular phones, near the system. All wireless
devices, whether they comply with the EMC standard or not, may emit electromagnetic
interferences and cause the system to malfunction when they are used nearby.

14
 Provide error messages for upper-level software
“Connect Error”
 In case of connection error, the “Connect Error” message is passed to the upper level
software

17
2. Product Introduction and Specification
2.1 Product Features
The HAD1717MC are wired digital flat panel detectors that have been designed for faster, more
streamlined approach to digital radiography systems. The HAD1717MC detector utilizes a
combination of propriety TFT glass and scintillators (CsI), and those and electronics are house in one
package. The detectors support an auto-trigger signal sensing technology that allows the detectors to
be used without generator integration.
The flat panel sensors of the HAD1717MC are fabricated using thin film technology based on
amorphous silicon technology. Electronically, the sensors are much like conventional photodiode
arrays. Each pixel in the array consists of a light-sensing photodiode and a switching Thin Film
Transistor (TFT) in the same electronic circuit. Amorphous silicon photodiodes are sensitive to visible
light, with a response curve roughly comparable to human vision. The sensitivity of amorphous silicon
photodiodes peaks in green wavelengths, well matched to scintillators such as CsI. The response has
the excellent linearity of a charge-integrating biased photodiode.
2.1.1 Indications for Use
Digital Flat Panel X-ray Detector, HAD1717MC is intended for use in general projection radiographic
applications wherever conventional screen-film systems or CR systems may be used. This device is
not intended for mammographic applications.
2.1.2 Contraindications
Local regulations should be reviewed before using those who have limitations in X-rays due to health
issues. Make sure to check the conditions of X-ray irradiation in advance. Not to be used for
mammography and direct cardiac application. Not to be used for infant and pregnant women.

2.3 Part Names and Functions
 Detector
 Data Cable Connector
This is a connector for wire communication and power supplying. The detector to the power supply
using the cable.
 Carbon Fiber Reinforced Plastic
The Part of the patient’s body to which an image is to be taken should be placed against the plate.
 Power Supply
Data Cable Connector
Front View : Carbon Fiber Reinforced Plastic

21
 LED indicator
When Status of LED is Green On, it means Power-On.
 Trigger Connector
This is a connector for synchronization between Detector and X-ray generator. Connect Power Supply
to the generator using trigger cable.
 Data Connector
This is a connector for wire communication and power supplying. 1giga-bit Ethernet signals,
synchronization signals between detector and X-ray generator and wires for power supplying are
integrated into the 25pins connector. Connect Power supply to the detector using data cable
 LAN Connector (RJ45)
This Connector is for 1giga-bit Ethernet communication between PC and Power Supply(Detector).
 Power Plug Connector
This is an AC Power Supply connector, and connector AC power supply cord.
Fuse : F3.15AH/250V
Switch : Power On/Off switch

3. Installation and Calibration

Agreement
Install
Close

28
 Product Set-Up
1) Integration
 Auto Trigger Mode
Automatically detects X-ray radiation without integration of the generator and the detector. So, any
connections are not required between the detector(Power Supply) and the generator.
※ Generator, PC are not included in this component.
 Line(Manual) Trigger Mode

By connecting(Trigger Cable) the generator and the detector, when the generator is ready for
operation, it sends a signal to the detector. When the detector receives this signal and is ready for
operation, it sends a signal back to the generator to emit radiation from the generator.
※ Generator, PC are not included in this component.

29
 Trigger Connection in Line(Manual) Trigger Mode
Trigger Cable Connector is positioned as the following picture.
<Power Supply : Trigger Cable Connector>
Trigger Cable signals consist of 2pairs named Exp_Reg / Exp_Reg_N, Exp_Ack_P / Exp_Ack.
Exp_Reg and Exp_Ack are available signals to each of both sides, detector and generator.
Signal Label Color In/Output
Exp_Reg Exp_Reg Green Output
Exp_Reg_N White Input
Exp_Ack Exp_Ack_P Black Input
Exp_Ack Red Output
<Trigger Signals Description>
The trigger cable is connected between the generator and the detector(Power Supply) as the
following picture.

30
Operation Sequence related to the trigger signals is descripted as the following Time Chart.
 If the generator is not ready for exposure during the detector ready
time(Step3. 0.6sec), add delay time using “Ready Delay” option.
“Ready Delay” time must be longer than 100msec, and its minimum unit
is 100msec

31
2) PC Set-Up
 Set-Up the Network as below
[Network Connection] > [Local Area Connection] > Click “Properties”
 Select [Internet Protocol Version 4(TCP/IP)] > Click “Properties

32
 Select [Use the following IP address], and then enter the IP address the Detector IP address.
 Abyz Detector’s default IP address is 2.2.22.101, Also you can use
2.2.22.10 ~ 2.2.22.101 detector IP. H&Abyz recommends 2.2.22.102 ~
2.2.22.254 for PC IP address and 255.255.255.0 for Subnet mask.

33
3) Acquisition Software(XAS) Set-Up
 Connect the Detector and turn on the power.
 Type the connected detector IP address at “Detector IP Address” if the IP address is
different with the connected detector IP address, and click “set”.
 Run “XAS.exe” located in “C:\XAS”. When the Detector is connected to PC, Network Status on
the software is changed from Red Cross” to “Green Check”.

34
 After checking the connectivity, select trigger mode between line(Manual) Trigger and Auto
Trigger.

35
 Select “Calibration” tap and click “Common Setting”
 Type required the value at “Window Time”. The window time must be longer than 100msec, and
its minimum unit is 100msec.
ADC resolution can be optionally selected between 14bit and 16bit. When “En_16bit” is
selected, 16bit image data is acquired from the detect. Click “Set Setting” after selecting
ADC resolution.
 When “Window Time” is shorter than X-ray Exposure Time, images will
not be properly acquired.
 Must click “Set Setting” after selecting ADC resolution.

36
3.2 Calibration
In order to properly acquire images, calibration must be performed. Without calibration, optimum
images cannot be acquired.
 H&abyz recommends to warm up the detector for 10 minutes after
turning on the power.
 Calibration should be performed at regular intervals, typically once
every six(6) months, or whenever the central beam of the X-ray source
has been moved relative to the detector.
 Dark Image Acquirement
 Click “Get Dark” to acquire a dark image in “Calibration” tap. “Preview” window pops up,
and a dark image is acquired. The acquired dark image is shown up in image file list.
 H&abyz recommends to use “Average Dark” option for better image
performance.
 Dark images are automatically acquired as the number of values at
“total dark frame” if “Average Dark” option is selected.

37
 Bright Image Acquirement and Cal Point Image Generation
 Click “Get Bright” to acquire bright images. Bright images must be acquired at each of 4
cal points. The acquired bright images are shown up in the image file list.
 H&Abyz recommends 4 cal points as the following table. If cal points
are not enough, some artifact can be shown up in the acquired images.
Cal Points 1 2 3 4
Median Value of pixels 14bit [LSB] 300 1000 7000 12000
Median Value of pixels 16bit [LSB] 1200 4000 28000 48000
 At least, two bright images must be acquired at each of cal points.
 In Auto Trigger Mode, X-ray Exposure time must be longer than
30msec. An image can not be acquired at shorter X-ray Exposure time
than 30msec.
 Do not expose X-ray when “Busy” message is displayed in “Preview”
pop-up window. Any Images can not be acquired during “Busy” state
although X-ray is exposed.
Expose X-ray when “Ready for Exposure” is shown up in “Preview”
window.

38
 Click “Generate Calibration Set” to generate Cal Point Images after acquiring bright
images. The generated Cal Point Images are listed up in the image file list and named as
“cBr_xxxxxA.raw”. “xxxxx” in the file name means the median value of pixels in the image.

39
 BPM Generation
 Click “Generate BPM” in BPM tap, and click “OK” in pop-up window to finish generating
the BPM.

40
4. Usage
4.1 Set-Up
 Image Set-Up
 In order to change the size of an image, use "Image Crop" in “Setting” tap. And click
“Save”.
 When “Image Crop” option in “Acquisition” tap is selected, Acquired
images can be cropped.

41
 Optionally, processing options can be selected. But select all processing options.
 When all processing options in “Acquisition” tap are selected, corrected
images can be acquired.
 Multi Detector Set Up
H&Abyz detector support “Multi Detector” function to connect a several detectors to one PC. This
function is useful when two detectors are integrated in a X-ray system.
 it could take a few seconds to change to another detector according to
PC condition. If customers repeatedly select others during changing the
detector, all detectors can be disconnected.

42
 Click “Edit” in “Setting” tap.
 Click “Add”. Additional Detector is listed up in “Detector List”.

43
 Type the added detector name at “Alias”, and change IP address and Image Size. To
apply the configuration changes, click “Apply”.
Click “Confirm” when the configuration is finished.
 Check another detector is added as the following picture, and select required detector.

44
4.2 Image Acquisition
 Check the network connection status and required processing options are selected in
“Acquisition” tap.

45
 Type image file name at “Image Name”, and click “Get Image” to acquire images. The
acquired images are shown up in the image file list.
 In Auto Trigger Mode, X-ray Exposure time must be longer than
30msec. An image can not be acquired at shorter X-ray Exposure time
than 30msec.
 Do not expose X-ray when “Busy” message is displayed in “Preview”
pop-up window. Any Images can not be acquired during “Busy” state
although X-ray is exposed.
Expose X-ray when “Ready for Exposure” is shown up in “Preview”
window.

4.3 Viewer

 H&abyz Viewer is popped up after double clicking the image.
① Image File List
② Image Bird-View
③ Pixel Values in the image
④ Image Histogram

- Min/Max Pixel Value

⑦ Vertical Profile
⑧ Horizontal Profile.
Double Click

47
 Click “Auto” for auto histogram windowing. Type window start value and end
value at “Window & Level” for manual histogram windowing.

48
5. Maintenance
5.1 Cleaning
 Clean the detector with IPA (Isopropyl-alcohol) when it is contaminated.
 Before cleaning the detector, turn off the power and separate the battery.
 Wear waterproof gloves to protect your hands from direct contact with IPA or any other
liquid.
 Do not pour or spray IPA directly on the detector. Use fabric or soft cloth moistened with
IPA to clean.
 Avoid getting IPA or any other liquid into the detector.
 After cleaning, wait until the IPA is dried completely.
5.2 Inspection
 In order to ensure that the detector is used safely and normally, please be sure to inspect
the product regularly before use.
 Please perform inspections based on the check list below.
Inspection List User Vendor Cycle
Check if cables are not damaged √ Daily
Check if plugs and connectors are not loose or damaged √ Daily
Check if cover or part is not damaged √ Daily
Check the LED indicator √ Daily
Re-Calibration √ Half Year
Check the performance of the product by doing test
shots with Phantom or resolution chart √ Yearly

49

 Fuse : F3.15AH/250V (5x20mm)
 Press the fuse box as the following picture and pull it out.
 Pull the fuses and replace with others.
 Ethernet Cable: UTP 4P 24AWG (CAT.6, straight-through)
 Power cord: 250 V~, 10 A, 0.75mm 2 x 3C (KR Spec.)

By ensuring this product is disposed of correctly, you will help prevent potential negative

6. Warranty
6.1 Warranty
If Buyer promptly notifies H&abyz or Seller regarding any parts that fail to perform as specified under
normal usage during the Warranty Period and H&abyz determines that such failure resulted from a
defect in materials or workmanship during the Warranty Period, then H&abyz, at its option, shall repair,
rebuild or adjust the affected parts.
H&abyz shall have no obligation for any defects to the extent that such defect arises out of (i) normal
and fair wear and tear or Product which has been modified without H&abyz’s approval, (ii) Product
which has not been installed in strict conformity to the H&abyz’s directions or which have been
subjected to electrical or other abuse, or damaged by improper handling, storage or use by Buyer or a
third party, (iii) use of Product in combination with devices or products not purchased from H&abyz;
(iv) use or application of Product in a field or in an environment for which such Product was not
designed or contemplated; (v) use of any parts or material not provided by H&abyz for warranty
service; or (vi) the third party’s maintenance not certified by H&abyz; or (vii) force majeure such as
natural disaster.
The remedies contained in this warranty are Buyer’s exclusive remedies. H&abyz shall not, in any
event or under any circumstances, be responsible for damages or other sums in excess of the total
purchase price actually paid by Buyer to Seller i.e., H&abyz or H&abyz’s authorized agent. Without
limiting the generality of the foregoing under no circumstance shall H&abyz be responsible or liable in
any regard with respect to damages from loss of use, loss of time, loss of data, inconvenience,
commercial loss, lost profits or savings, or other incidental, special or consequential damages claimed
by Buyer to arise out of the use or inability to use the Product, even if Buyer has been advised of the
possibility of such damages.
In the event that the product is returned to H&abyz after the warranty has expired, H&abyz reserves
the right to invoice a reasonable fee for the repair services provided to Buyer.
H&abyz shall make the sole final determination about whether the fail to perform occurred in normal
usage (under warranty) or not (excluded from warranty). If the authorized agent or the Buyer doesn’t
accept the result of H&abyz’s investigation, the burden of proof is on them.

PART 2. Service Manual

53
This Service Manual gives additional instruction for setting up the detector.
1. CS Manager Instruction
1.1 Detector MAC & IP Address Set Up
1) Detector IP Address Set Up
 Connect the Detector and turn on the power.
 Launch the CS Manager and select the "IP_Change" tab.
 Enter the IP address you want to change from 2.2.22.10 ~ 2.2.22.101 and click "Set" button.
(The default IP address of the detector is 2.2.22.101)
 If "IP Setting Done" message is displayed in the popup window, IP address change is
successful. If "Work exceeded time" message is displayed, IP address change fails.
 After changing the IP address, the detector must be rebooted.

54
2) Detector MAC Address Set Up
 Connect the Detector and turn on the power.
 Launch the CS Manager and select the "MAC_Change" tab.
 Enter the MAC address you want to change and click "Set" button.
 (The default MAC address of the detector is “1E:ED:19:27:1A:B3”)
 If "MAC Setting Done" message is displayed in the popup window, MAC address change is
successful. If "Work exceeded time" message is displayed, MAC address change fails.
 After changing the MAC address, the detector must be rebooted.

55
1.2 Firmware, FPGA Update
1) Firmware Update
 Connect the Detector and turn on the power.
 Launch the CS Manager and select the "FW_Update" tab.
 Click the "..." button and select the firmware file.
 If "please Reboot" message is displayed in the popup window, FW update is successful. If
"Work exceeded time" message is displayed, FW update fails.
 After FW Update, the detector must be rebooted.

56
2) FPGA Update
 Connect the detector and turn on the power.
 Launch the CS Manager and select the "FPGA_Update" tab.
 Click the "..." button and select the FPGA file.
 If "Please Reboot" message is displayed in the popup window, FPAG update is successful. If
"Work exceeded time" message is displayed, FPGA update fails.
 After FPGA Update, the detector must be rebooted.

57
1.3 RTC Set Up
1) RTC Set Up
 Connect the Detector and turn on the power.
 Launch the CS Manager and select the “RTC Set " tab.
 Click the Update button to set the Detector time to the Window's current time.
 If "RTC Set done" message is displayed in the popup window, RTC Set Up is successful. If
"Work exceeded time" message is displayed, RTC Set Up fails.
 The time set on the detector is displayed in the program.

58
1.4 Default IP Set Up
1) Default IP Set Up
 Connect the Detector and turn on the power.
 Launch the CS Manager and select the “Default IP" tab.
 Enter the IP address of the detector to be connected and click the "Set" button.
 When CS_Manager attempts to connect to the detector, it tries to connect to the IP address
set in Default IP

59
2. Troubleshooting
2.1 LAN Connection Issue
1) Check the Power
 Check the Data Cable and the Power cord are connected properly
 Check if the power led of the Power Supply is on
2) Check PC Set Up
 Make sure that the IP address is set to ”2.2.22.102 ~ 2.2.22.254” in “Internet Protocol
Version4(TCP/IP)”.

60
2.2 Auto Trigger Mode
 To use Auto Trigger Mode, customers must keep a several
requirements. When the requirements are not met, image acquisition
could be failed.
When image acquisition is failed, please check the following requirement for Auto Trigger mode.
① Keep Min X-ray Exposure time = 30ms
② Expose X-ray when “Ready for Exposure” message is displayed in “Preview” window.
Do not expose X-ray when the message is “Busy”
